01. පොල්‌ වගාකිටමේ මණ්බලයේ ව්‍යාප්ති හා
සංවරධන වැඩසටහන්‌

02. ආදටශ පොල්‌ උයන්‌ හා තවාන්‌ සංවරධන අංශය මගින්‌

04. අභ්‍යන්තර වගණන අංශය

05. මූල්‍ය කළමනාකරණ අංශය

1. පොල්‌ වගාකිරීමේ මණ්ඩලයේ ව්‍යාප්ති හා
සංවර්ධන වැඩසටහන්‌

පොල්‌ වගාකිරීමේ මණ්ඩලයේ ප්‍රධාන සංවර්ධන වැඩසටහන්‌ හා ව්‍යාප්ති වැඩසටහන්‌ සෘජුවම

ගානි සිතියම්‌ ගත කිරීමේ වැඩසටහන ක්‍රියාත්මක කරන ලදි. මේ යටතේ සියලුම ප්‍රාදේශීය කාර්යාල බල ප්‍රදෝශවල
පොල්‌ වගාවට හානි කරන ප්‍රධාන කෘමීන්‌ වන රතු කුරුමිණයා, කළු කුරුමිණියා, පොල්‌ මයිටාවා සහ පොල්‌ දළඹුවා

1.3. “කප්රුක ආයෝජන” ණය යෝජනා ක්‍රමය.

1.4.3. කප්රුක සමිති සාමාජිකයින්‌ සඳහා පුහුණු වැඩසටහන්‌ කියාත්මක කිරීම.

2019 වර්ෂයේ ඔක්තෝම්බර්‌ මස 08 වන දින ජාතික වැවිලි කළමනාකරණ ආයතනයේ මෙහෙයවීම සහ ප්‍රතිපාදන
යටතේ කොහු ලණු ආශ්‍රයෙන්‌ පාපිසි නිෂ්පාදනය පිළිබද එක්‌ දින පුහුණුවක්‌ පැවැත්විණ. මෙම පුහුණුව පොල්‌
වගාකිරීමේ මණ්ඩලයට අයන්‌ මාතර ප්‍රාදෝශීය කාර්යාලයේ පැවැත්විණ. මෙම ප්‍රදර්ශනය සඳහා මාතර, ගාල්ල සහ
හම්බන්තොට ප්‍රාදෝශීය කාර්යාල වලට අයත්‌ කප්රුක සමිති සාමාජිකයන්‌ මෙම පුහුණු වැඩසටහනට සහභාගී විය.

1.4.4. ක්ෂේත්‍ර අධ්‍යාපන චංරිකා

මාතලේ ප්‍රාදේශීය කාර්යාලයට අයන්‌ ගලේවෙල කප්රුක සමිති සාමාජිකයින්‌ හට පොල්‌ ඉඩම්‌ වලින්‌ ලබන ආදායම
ඉහළ නැංවීම සදහා පොල්‌ වගාව අතර අතුරු බෝගයක්‌ ලෙස ටොම්‌. ඡජේ.සී. අඹ ප්‍රභේදය වගා කිරීම පිළිබඳ පුහුණු
වැඩසටහනක්‌ සහ ක්ෂේත්‍ර අධ්‍යයනයක්‌ සිදුකරන ලදී.

1.4.5. කප්රුක සමිති විමර්ෂණය සිදූ කිරීම
කප්රුක අරමුදලේ විවිධ ආයෝජනයන්‌ සිදුව ඇති A හා B ශ්‍රේණවල කප්රුක සමිති පිලිබඳ වියිමන්‌ විමර්ශනයක්‌ සෑම

වර්ෂයකම සිදු කරනු ලබයි. මෙම කටයුත්ත ක්‍රියාත්මක කිරීම සඳහා ඒ ඒ ප්‍රාදේශීය කාර්යාල මට්ටමින්‌ නිලධාරීන්‌ 05
දෙනෙකු ලෙස පුහුණු කර ඇත. එසේම ටියිමන්‌ විමර්ශන ආකෘතීන්‌ අනුගමනය කරමින්‌ අදාල විමර්ශන කියාවලිය
කියාත්මක කර ඇත. කප්රුක සමිති 50 ක්‌ 2010 වර්ෂයේදී විමර්යන කර අවසන්‌ කර ඇත.

L.4.0. කප්රුක සම්පත්‌ මධ්‍යස්ථාන පිඟිටූවීම

කප්රුක සමිති සඳහා මෙහෙයුම්‌ මධ්‍යස්ථානයක්‌ ලෙසින්‌, ඔවුන්ගේ අමුදවය එකතුකරන මධ්‍යස්ථානයක්‌ ලෙසත්‌,
තොරතුරු මධ්‍යස්ථානයක්‌ ලෙසත්‌ සහ ප්‍රජා වෘත්තීය මධ්‍යස්ථානයක්‌ ලෙසත්‌ වවුනියාව ප්‍රාදේශීය කාර්යාලයේ මෙම
සම්පත්‌ මධ්‍යස්ථානයක්‌ 2010 වර්ෂයේදී පිහිටුවා ඇත.

1.5. පොල්‌ සංවර්ධන පුහුණු මධ්‍යස්ථානය

හැදින්‌ වීම

පොල්‌ සංවර්ධන පුහුණු මධ්‍යස්ථානය පොල්‌ පර්යේෂණ ආයතනයට යාබද බණ්ඩිරිප්පුව වත්ත, ලුණුවිල යන ස්ථානයේ
පිහිටා ඇත.

පුහුණු සදහා පැමිණ පුහුණු කණ්ඩායම්‌ වල පුද්ගලයින්‌ 344 දෙනෙකු සඳහා ද නේවාසික පහසුකම්‌ සලසා ඇත.

තවද පොල්‌ සංවර්ධන පුහුණු මධ්‍යස්ථාන නේවාසිකාගාරය බාහිර ආයතනයන්හි ඉල්ලීම්‌ අනුව පුහුණු කණ්ඩායම්‌ වලට

නේවාසික පහසුකම්‌ සපයා නැති අවස්ථාවලදී බාහිර ආයතන සඳහා නේවාසික පහසුකම්‌ සපයනු ලැබේ. 20109 වර්ෂයේදී

තෙල්‌ නිෂ්පාදනය, පොල්‌ පැල නිෂ්පාදනය,අතුරු වගා පැල නිෂ්පාදනය,කප්තුරුපාය අලෙවිසැල්‌ පවත්වාගෙනයාම
සිදුකරයි. එසේම ආදර්ශ පොල්‌ උයන්‌ වල විභවය අනුව වී වගා කිරීම,රබර්‌ වගා කිරිම, විලෝපිත මයිටා පැකට්‌
නිෂ්පාදනය, පොල්‌ සංචාරක ව්‍යාපෘතිය හං ග්ලිරිසීඩියා වගා ව්‍යාපෘති ක්‍රියාත්මක කරන ලදී. පොල්‌ වගා පාදක ලාභදායී
ව්‍යාපාරයක්‌ ලෙස ආදර්ශන මට්ටමින්‌ ආදර්ශ පොල්‌ උයන්‌ පචත්වාගෙනයාම ප්‍රධාන අරමුණවේ. එසේම පොල්‌
සංවර්ධන පුහුණු මධ්‍යස්ථානය මහින්‌ පොල්‌ වගාකරුවන්‌,පාසැල්‌ සිසුන්‌, විශ්ට විද්‍යාල සිසුන්‌, රාජ්‍ය හා පෞද්ගලික
ආයතන වල නිලධාරීන්‌ හා කෘෂි කාර්මික සංවිධාන වල සමිති සාමාජිකයින්‌ සඳහා සිදු කරනු ලබන පුහුණු වැඩසටහන්‌
වලදී දැනුවත්‌ කිරීම්‌ සිදු කරයි. එසේම මෙම ආදර්්‍යයපොල්‌ උයන්‌ මඟින්‌ පුහුණුවන්නන්ට පොල්‌ වගාව ලාභදායීව

ආදර්ශ පොල්‌ උයන්වල නිමැවුම්‌ ලෙස උසස්‌ තත්වයේ බිජ පොල්‌ , පොල්‌ පැල ,මාළු පොල්‌ ,කොප්පරා ,පොල්‌ කටු

අඟුරු ,එළ කිරි ,මී කිරි ,යොෝගට , කිරි ටො , බිත්තර, එළවළු,පලතුරු,කුළු බඩුූ,රබර්‌,අතුරු හොෝග පැල, වී හා විලොෝපිත

2.1.17. අරු වගා වැඩසටහන

පොල්‌ වගාව සිදුකරනු ලබන භූමිවල පොල්‌ වගාවේ පරතරය හේතුවෙන්‌ භූමි භාවිතයෙන්‌ 2/3 ඉඩ
ප්‍රමාණයක්‌ ඉතිරිවන අතර මෙම ඉඩකඩ ප්‍රමාණය තුල වෙනත්‌ වගා සිදු කල හැක.අවුරුදු5 ට අඩු හා අවුූරුදු35 ට වැසි
පොල්‌ වගාව තනි වගාවක්‌ ලෙස සිදු කරන භූමි වල අතුරු වගා කිරීම සිදුකිරීමේ හැකියාව ඇත. ඒ අනුව එම ඉඩකඩ
ප්‍රමාණය භාවිතා කොට කෙටිකාලීන හෝග හා දිගු කාලීන හොග අළුතින්‌ වගාකිරීමන්‌ පවතින අතුරු වගා නඩත්තු
කිරීමත්‌ සිදුකර ඇත අතුරු වගා ලෙස කෙටි කාලීන එළවළු වර්ග, අල වර්ග, ඹෟෂධ වර්ග, කුළුබඩු වර්ග, මාෂ හෝොෝග,
ධාන්‍ය හා පලතුරු හොෝග වගාකර ඇත. 2010 වර්ෂයේ අතුරු වගා මහින්‌ රුැ.2512036.00 ක ආදායමක්‌ හා රු 504086.62

ක ලාභයක්‌ ලබා ඇත.

ගර්ටලන්ඩ්‌ , ලේනව ,කොහොඹාන ,පලෙයි හා නාගන්සොෝලආදර්ශ පොල්‌ උයන්වල වී වගා වැඩ සටහන 2010
වර්ෂයේදී ක්‍රියාත්මක විය. ඉන්‌ ආදර්ශ පොල්‌ උයන්‌ 03 ක අක්කර 85.75 වී වගාව අඳ ගොවීන්‌ මඟින්‌ සිදුකර ඇති අතර

බැටළු පාලනය

එළු පාලනය

ආදර්ශ පොල්‌ උයනේ භූමි ඵලදායීතාවය ඉහළ නැංවීම සිදුකරයි. ආදර්ශ පොල්‌ උයනේ පවතින විභවය අනුව තෝරාගත්‌

2.2. තවාන්‌ අංශය

2.2.1. පොල්‌ පැළ නිෂ්පාදන සහ පැළ නිකුත්‌ කිරීමේ වැඩසටහන

දිවයිනේ වගාකිරීමට අවශ්‍ය උසස්‌ තත්වයේ පොල්‌ පැළ නිෂ්පාදනය කර වගාකරුවනට සැපයීම පොල්‌ වගාකිරීමේ
මණ්ඩලයේ ප්‍රධාන කාර්යයන්ගෙන්‌ එකකි. වා්‍යාජ්ති හං සංවර්ධන අංශයේ සැලසුම්වලට අනුව වර්ෂයේ පැළ
නිෂ්පාදනයට අවශ්‍ය බිජ පොල්‌ තවාන්‌ වෙත සැපයීමට සැලසුමිකිරීම, මෙහෙයවීම හං සම්බන්ධීකරණය, පැළ
නිෂ්පාදනය ආදර්ශ පොල්‌ උයන්‌ හා තවාන්‌ සංවර්ධන අංශය මගින්‌ සිදුකෙරේ. පොල්‌ පැළ නිෂ්පාදන කාර්යය සඳහා
ප්‍රාදෝශගීය කාර්යාල, තවාන්‌, ආදර්ශ පොල්‌ උයන්‌ හා මීගමුව බිජ පොල්‌ ඒකකය ප්‍රධාන වශයෙන්‌ දායකවේ.

ප්‍රාදෝශීය කළමණාකරුවන්ගේ මඟ පෙන්වීම හා නේවාසික තවාන්‌ භාරකරුගේ සෘජු අයික්ෂණය යටතේ පොල්‌ පැළ
නිෂ්පාදනය ප්‍රධාන කාර්යය කරගත්‌ පොල්‌ පැළ තවාන්‌ 39 ක්‌ මහින්‌ හා ආදර්ශ පොල්‌ උයන්‌ කළමණාකරුගේ සෘජු
අයීක්ෂණය හා මඟ පෙන්වීම යටතේ ආදර්ශ පොල්‌ උයන්‌ තුල ස්ථාපිත පොල්‌ පැළ තවාන්‌ 12 ක්‌ මඟින්‌ වගාකරුවන්ට
අවශ්‍යලසස්‌ තත්වයේ ගුණාත්මක පොල්‌ පැළ නිෂ්පාදනය කෙරේ.

පොල්‌ වගාකරුවන්ට පහසුවෙන්‌ පොල්‌ පැළ සැපයීමේ අරමුණන්‌ මණ්ඩලයේ පොල්‌ පැළ තවාන්‌ දිවයින පුරා ස්ථාපිත
කර ඇති අතර, ඉන්‌ වැඩි ප්‍රමාණයක්‌ පොල්‌ වගාව බහුල ලෙස ව්‍යාප්තව ඇති වයඹ පලාත තුල පවතී. ප්‍රාදෝගීය පොල්‌
තවාන්චල කටයුතු ඒ ඒ ප්‍රාදෝශීය කාර්යාල මඟින්‌ පාලනය හා නඬත්තුව සිදූ කරනු ලබයි. පොල්‌ වගාකිරීමේ මණ්ඩලය
මඟින්‌ 2010වර්ෂයේදී පොල්‌ පැළ නිෂ්පාදනය කරන ලද ආකාරය පහතින්‌ දක්වා ඇත.

2.2.2. 2010 වර්ෂයේ පොල්‌ පැළ ඉලක්කයන්‌
2010 වර්ෂයේ පොල්‌ වගාකිරීමේ මණ්ඩලයේ කළමනාකාරීත්වය මඟින්‌ පොල්‌ පැළ මි. 2.01ක්‌ නිෂ්පාදනය කිරීමට
ඉලක්ක කරන ලදී.

2.2.3. පොල්‌ වගාකිරීමේ මණ්ඩලයේ පොල්‌ පැළ තවාන්‌ මහින්‌ නිෂ්පාදනය කර 2010 වසර තුල නිකුත්‌
කරන ලද පොල්‌ පැළ ප්‍රුමානයන්‌

මේ අනුව 20109 වසර තුළ පොල්‌ වගා කිරීමේ මණ්ඩලයේ ආදර්ශ පොල්‌ උයන්‌ හා තවාන්‌ සංවර්ධන අංශය යටතේ
පාළනය වන දිවයින පුරා ව්‍යාජතව පවතින පොල්‌ පැළ තවාන්‌ මහින්‌, ජානමය උසස්‌ පොල්‌ පැළ නිෂ්පාදනය කර පැළ

කප්සුවය වර්ග අනුව පොල්‌ පැළ සිටවා ක්ෂේත්‍ර ආදර්ශණයක්‌ සකස්‌ කිරීම.

2.23. කහ කුන්දිරා පැළ සිටවීම.
ඉදිරියේදී දෙමුහුන්‌ බීජ උයන්‌ ලෙස වැඩි දියුණු කිරීමේ අරමුණින්‌ තවාන්‌ වල කහ කුන්දිරා පැළ සිටවීම.

2.3. මීගමුව බීජ නිෂ්පාදන ඒකකය.

දිවයින පුරා වගාකිරීම සදහා උසස්‌ නිෂ්පාදන හැකියාවෙන්‌ යුත්‌, උසස්‌ තත්ත්වයේ පොල්‌ පැළ වගාකරුවන්‌ වෙත ලබා
දීමේ අරමුණන්‌ පොල්‌ පර්යේෂණ ආයතනයේ අධීක්ෂණය සහිතව උසස්‌ මවි ශාක තෝරා ලබා ගන්නා බීජ පොල්‌
සියලුම තවාන්‌ හා ආදර්ශ පොල්‌ උයන්‌ වෙත ප්‍රවාහනය කර සැපයීම ප්‍රධාන කාර්ය වේ.

එයට අමතරව වාර්ෂික බිජ පොල්‌ අවශ්‍යතා සපුරා ගැනීමට අවශ්‍ය ක්‍රමෝපාය සැලසුම්‌ සකස්‌ කිරීමට දායකත්වය ලබාදී
එම සැලසුම්‌ ක්‍රියාත්මක කිරීම, පොල්‌ වගාකරුවන්ට අවශ්‍ය යෙදවුම්‌ හා සැපයුම්‌ සේවාවන්‌ සඳහා පහසුකම්‌ සැපයීම හා
මෙහෙයවීමන්‌ මෙම ඒකකය සතු අනෙකුන්‌ කාර්යයන්‌ වේ. මෙම සියලූ කටයුතු සිදූ කරනු ලබන්නේ බිජ නිෂ්පාදන
ඒකකය විසින්‌ වන අතර, ඒ සදහා එම ඒකකය සතුව අවශ්‍ය යටිතල පහසුකම්‌ සහ පලපුරුදු ක්ෂේත්‍ර කාර්ය
මණ්ඩලයක්ද අනුයුක්තව සිටී.

ඒ ඒ දිස්ත්‍රික්කවල ක්‍රියාත්මක කරන ලද පොල්‌ වගාකිරීමේ වැඩසටහන්‌ සඳහා අවශ්‍ය වූ පොල්‌ පැළ ප්‍රමාණය ප්‍රාදේශීය
කාර්යාල අනුව විවිධ වන අතර, ප්‍රදේශයේ වගාකරුවන්ගේ පොල්‌ පැළ ඉල්ලීමද සලකා බැලූවිට ප්‍රාදේශීය කාර්යාලවල
පොල්‌ පැළ අවශ්‍යතාව එකිනෙකට වෙනස්වේ. වාර්ෂිකව තම ප්‍රදෝ්‍යශයේ පොල්‌ පැළ අවශ්‍යතාවය ප්‍රාදේශීය
කළමණාකරුවන්‌ විසින්‌ ප්‍රධාන කාර්යාලයට දැනුම්‌ දෙනු ලබන අතර, ප්‍රාදේශීය කාර්යාලවල පොල්‌ පැළ අවශ්‍යතාව හා
තවානේ බිජ පොල්‌ ධාරිතාවය, මානව සම්පත්‌ සුලභතාවය හා යටිතල පහසුකම්‌ පවතින ප්‍රමාණය ද සලකා බලා ප්‍රධාන

4. මානව සම්පත්‌ කළමනාකරණ පද්ධතිය ස්ථාපනය

5. කාර්යක්ෂමතා කඩඉම්‌ පරික්ෂණ

පැවැත්වීම සඳහා ජාතික ශ්‍රම අධ්‍යයන ආයතනය වෙත සියලූ කටයුතු භාරදීමත්‌, එමගින්‌ කාර්ය මණ්ඩලය සදහා
උස්සවීම්‌ අවස්ථා සහ සේවය ස්ථීර වීම්‌ ඇතුළු ශ්‍රේණ උසස්වීම්‌ සදහා අවකාශයන්‌ පුළුල්කර දීම.

පොල්‌ වගාකිරීමේ මණ්ඩලයේ සංවර්ධන කාර්යන්‌ සපුරා ගැනීම සඳහා ඉහත සඳහන්‌ ප්‍රවාහන සංචිතය සතු
සම්පත්‌ අඩු පිරිවැයකින්‌ යොදවා ගැනීමට පරිපාලන හා මානව සම්පත්‌ කළමනාකරණ අංශය කටයුතු කර

TD.

එසේම ප්‍රවාහන සංචිතය මගින්‌ සේවක සුභසාධනය හං අභිප්‍රේරණය වෙනුවෙන්‌ පහත සඳහන්‌ පරිදි කටයුතු
කර ඇත.

 සේවකයන්ගේ හා ඥාතීන්ගේ අවමංගල්‍ය කටයුතු සඳහා සහන පදනම යටතේ ප්‍රවාහන පහසුකම්‌
සැපයීම.

 වාර්ෂික අධ්‍යාපන, සුහද හමු හා විනොෝද චාරිකා වෙනුවෙන්‌ සහන පදනම යටතේ ප්‍රවාහන
පහසුකම්‌ සැපයීම.

 සේවකයන්ගේ විශේෂ අවශ්‍යතා (විවාහ උත්සව) සඳහා සහන මිල ගණන්‌ අයකර ගැන්මේ පදනම
යටතේ සංචිත වාහන ලබාදීම.

 වා්‍යාපෘති කටයුතු සඳහා සංචිත වාහන යොදවා එම කටයුතු සාර්ථක කරගැනීමට අවශ්‍ය කටයුතු
කර ඇත. (වැලිගම ව්‍යාපෘතිය, තේ සමඟ පොල්‌ ව්‍යාපෘතිය)

ඉදිකිරිම්‌ අත්පත්‌ කර ගැනීම්‌

මණ්ඩලීය ප්‍රාග්ධන වත්කම්‌ අත්පත්‌ කර ගැන්ම හං ප්‍රාග්ධන වත්කම්‌ වල නඬත්තූ කටයුතු මේ යටතේ
ආවරණය කෙරේ. ඒ අනුව පහත දක්වා ඇති ප්‍රධාන ඉදිකිරීම්‌ කටයුතු 2010 වර්ෂය තුළදී ආරම්භ කර නීම
කිරීමට හැකි විය.

 මාතලේ නව කාර්යාල ගොඩනැගිල්ලේ දෙවන අදියරෙහි ඉදිකිරීම්‌ ආරම්භ කර අවසන්‌ අදියර දක්වා
නීමකිරීම.

 යාපනය සම්පත්‌ මධ්‍යස්ථානය සහ කාර්යාල ගොඩනැගිල්ලේ ඉදිකිරීම්‌ කටයුතු අවසන්‌ අදියර දක්වා
නීමකිරීම.

— පොළොන්නරුව නිලධාරී නිල නිවාසයේ ඉදිකිරීම්‌ ආරම්භ කර අවසන්‌ අදියර දක්වා නීමකිරීම.

 ප්‍රාදේශිය කාර්යාලයන්හගි වැසිකිළි පද්ධතිය” කාර්යාල ගොඩනැඟිලි නිළ නිවාසයන්‌ ගි
අළුත්වැඩියාවන්‌ සිදු කිරිම.

 ලුණුවිල පොල්‌ සංවර්ධන පුහුණු මධ්‍යස්ථානයේ නේවාසිකාගාරය සහ කාර්යාල ගොඩනැඟිලි
අළුත්වැඩියා කිරීම.

 කළුතර නේවාසිකාගාරය පිහිටි ඉඩම වටා වැට ගැසීම.
 කල්පිටිය පොල්‌ සංවර්ධන නිළ නිවාසය වටා භඟුමියෙහි වැට ගැසීම.

මේ අනුව පරිපාලන හා මානව සම්පත්‌ කළමනාකරණ අංශය, 2010 වර්ෂය තුල සේවකයන්‌ පුහුණු කිරීම හා
අභිපෝරණ කටයුතු කරමින්ද, ප්‍රාග්ධන ඉදිකිරීම්‌ අත්පත්කරගැනීම්‌ සංවර්ධනය හා පහසුකම්‌ අළුත්වැඩියා
කිරීමේ කටයුතු හා නඩත්තු සේවා පවත්වාගැනීමට කටයුතු කරමින්ද, පවතින අවම සම්පත්‌ උපරිම ලෙස
කළමනාකරණය කරමින්ද, මණ්ඩලයේ ප්‍රමුඛ කාර්යභාරය වන පොල්‌ වගාව ව්‍යාප්ත කරලීමේ කටයුත්ත
සඳහා මනා සහයෝගයක්‌ ලබාදීමට කටයුතු කර ඇත.

oe miko)eloylo>lehilts)


4.0. අභා්‍යන්තර විගණන අංශය

4.1. අභ්‍යන්තර විගණනයේ අරමුණ
පොල්‌ වගාකිරීමේ මණ්ඩලය ළඟාකර ගැනීමට අපේක්ෂිත දැක්ම, මෙහෙවර,පරමාර්ථ ළඟා කර ගැනීම සදහා

සංවිධානයේ කටයුතු කර තිබේද යන්න සහ අභ්‍යන්තර පාලන ක්‍රියාවලිය වර්ෂය පුරා කාර්යක්ෂමව හා
ඵලදායීව තිබෙද යන්න හා වත්කම්‌ ආරක්ෂා කර ගැනීමට අවශ්‍ය කටයුතු යොදමින්‌ ප්‍රාදෝශිය ඒකක අතර මනා
සම්බන්ධිකරණයක්‌ පවත්වාගෙන යන්නේදැයි පිළිබඳව සිදුකරනු ලබන ඇගයීමක්‌.

4.2. මෙම වර්ෂය තුළ සිදුකරන ලද අභා්‍යන්තර විගණන පරික්ෂණ
අභ්‍යන්තර විගණන විෂය පථයට අදාළ කාර්යභාරය හං රාජකාරි ඉතාමත්‌ ගුණාත්මක තත්වයකින්‌ අඛණ්ඩ

පදනමක්‌ මත 20109 වර්ෂය තුල ඉටුකර ඇත.

4.2.1. ප්‍රධාන කාර්යාලයයේ සිදුකරන ලද විගණන පරික්ෂණ

1. 2016 පොලි බෑග්‌ ටෙන්ඩරය සම්බන්ධ විගණන පරික්ෂණය

2. 208100140329975 අංක දරණ මුදල්‌ පොත්‌ සම්බන්ධ විගණන පරීක්ෂණය

3. වැටුප්‌ අවප්‍රමාණය වීම සම්බන්ධ විගණන පරික්ෂණය
4. ප්‍රධාන කාර්යාලයේ ගබඩාව පිළිබඳ විගණන පරික්ෂණය

5. 2016 වර්ෂයේ පොහොර සඳහා ගෙවීම්‌ කිරීම වල නිරික්ෂණ සම්බන්ධ වාර්තාව

4.2.2. ප්‍රාදෝේගීය කාර්යාල වල සිදුකරන ලද විගණන පරික්ෂණ

4.2.5. එසේ අනාවරණය වූ පොදු වැරදි හා අඩුපාඩු

ප්‍රධාන කාර්යාලයේ මුදල්‌ පොත්‌ නඩත්තු කිරීමේ අඩුපාඩු.

ප්‍රාදෝගීය කාර්යාලය වල, ආදර්ශ පොල්‌ උයන්‌ සහ තවාන්‌ වල මුදල්‌ පොත්‌ නඩත්තු කිරීමේ අඩුපාඩු.

සමහර බාහිර ඒකක වල අත්තිකාරම්‌ ලේඛනය නිවැරදි ආකෘතියකට අනුකුලව නඩත්තු කර නොමැතිවීම.

සමහර ප්‍රාදේශීය කාර්යාලය වල, ආදර්ශ පොල්‌ උයන්‌ සහ තවාන්‌ වල පොල්‌ පැල ආදායම්‌ ප්‍රමාද වී

බැංකුගත කිරීම.

ප්‍රාදෝගීය කාර්යාල වල වවුචර්‌ සකස්‌ අඩුපාඩු.

තවාන්‌ වල දොරටු අවසර ලේඛන විධිමන්වච නඩත්තු නොකිරීම.

ප්‍රාදේශීය කාර්යාලය වල, ආදර්ශ පොල්‌ උයන්‌ සහ තවාන්‌ වල ප්‍රසම්පාදන කටයුතු වල අඩුපාඩු.

තොග පොත්‌ නඩත්තුකිරීමේ අඩුපාඩු.

ප්‍රාදේශීය කාර්යාල වල ධාවන සටහන්‌ පොන්‌ නඩත්තු කිරීමේ අඩුපාඩු.

10. සහනාධාර පදනම මත පොල්‌ පැළ නිකුත්කිරීම සම්බන්ධ අභා්‍යන්තර පාලන ක්‍රමවල අඩුපාඩු

මෙම වර්ෂය තුල විගණන හා කළමනාකරණ කමිටු රැස්වීම්‌ 04 ක්‌ පවත්වා ඇත.

05. මූල්‍ය කළමනාකරණ අංශය

5.1. ගිණුම්‌ ප්‍රකාශය

පොල්‌ වගා කිරීමේ මණ්ඩලයේ සමස්ත කාර්යයන්‌ 1071 අංක 40 දරණ පොල්‌ සංවර්ධන පනතේ වියිවිධානයන්ට
අනුකුලව, නියමිත චක්‍රලේඛ මුදල්‌ රෙගුලාසි වලට යටන්ව ග්‍රී ලංකා රාජ්‍ය මූලා්‍ය ගිණුමිකරණ ප්‍රමිති අනුව 2019.12.31
දිනෙන්‌ අවසන්‌ වාර්ෂික මූල්‍ය වාර්තා ඉදිරිපත්‌ කර ඇත.

දීප ව්‍යාප්තව ප්‍රාදෝගීය කාර්යාල 19ක්ද පුහුණු මධ්‍යස්ථාන 3ක්‌ සහිත සම්බන්යීකරණ ජාලයක්‌ තුළ තවාන්‌ 30කින්‌ සහ
ආදර්ශ පොල්‌ උයන්‌ 12කින්‌ සපුරාගත යුතු ඉලක්ක සාක්ෂාත්‌ කර ගැනීමටද ජාතික මට්ටමේ සංවර්ධන ව්‍යාපෘතීන්‌ සහ
වැඩසටහන්‌ ක්‍රියාත්මක කිරීමට උචිත වන්නා වූ මූල්‍ය ඇස්තමේන්තු සකස්‌ කිරීම, සැළසුම්‌ කිරීම, මෙහෙයවීම හා පාලනය
කිරීම, ලේඛනගත කිරීම වාර්තා කිරීම හා පුරෝකථනය කිරීම මූල්‍ය කළමනාකරණ අංශයේ ප්‍රමුඛ ක්‍රියාදාමයයි.

නියෝජ්‍ය සාමාන්‍යාධිකාරී (මූල්‍ය කළමනාකරණ) ගේ මෙහෙයවීම හා මගපෙන්වීම යටතේ මූල්‍ය කළමනාකරණ අංශයේ
සහකාර සාමාන්‍යාධිකාරී (මූල්‍ය කළමනාකරණ), ගණකාධිකාරී (මූල්‍ය), ගණකායිකාරී (ආදර්ශ පොල්‌ උයන්‌),ගිණුම්‌
නිළධාරී වශයෙන්‌ හා සහයක කාර්යය මණ්ඩලය දීප ව්‍යාප්තව ප්‍රාදෝශීය කාර්යාල තුළ මූල්‍ය කටයුතු මෙහෙයවීම, වාර්තා
කිරීම හා පාලනය කිරීම සිදුකරනු ලබයි.

2019 වර්ෂයේ මණ්ඩලයේ ඇස්තමේන්තු වලට අදාලව පුනරාවර්ථන වැය ශිර්ෂය යටතේ රැ මිලියන 460.00 ක්‌
රු.මිලියන 568.00 ප්‍රාග්ධන වැය ශීර්ෂය යටතේ මහා භාණ්ඩාගාරය මඟින්‌ ප්‍රතිපාදන ලබා දී ඇත.

වැවිලි කර්මාන්ත අමාත්‍යාංශය වෙනුවෙන්‌ පොල්‌ වගාව නගා සිටුවීම සඳහා වූ ව්‍යාපෘති පවත්වාගෙන යාමට පොල්‌
වගාකිරීමේ මණ්ඩලය කටයුතු කරයි. ඒ අනුව කප්රුක පුරවර අරමුදල සඳහා රු. මිලියන 17.1090ක්ද, පොල්‌ කොළ
මැලවීමේ හා කුණුවීමේ මර්ධන වැඩසටහන සඳහා රු. මිලියන 15.73 1ක්ද, පොල්‌ වගාවේ කෘමි හානි සිතියම්ගත කිරීමේ
ව්‍යාපෘතිය වෙනුවෙන්‌ රු. මිලියන 6.6070ක්ද, පුහුණු ගුමික බලකා වැඩසටහන සඳහා රු. මිලියන 15.855ක්ද, මයිටා පාලන
ව්‍යාපෘතිය සඳහා රු. මිලියන 3.300ක ප්‍රතිපාදන ලබා දී ඇත.

ගාල්ල මාතර හා හම්බන්තොට දිස්ත්‍රික්කයන්‌ තුළ ව්‍යාප්ත පොල්‌ වගාවට සම්බන්ධයෙන්‌ පැතිර ඇති කොළ මැළවීමේ
රෝගය මර්ධනය කිරීමට හා මැඩ පැවැත්වීම සඳහා වැවිලි කර්මාන්ත අමාත්‍යාංශයෙන්‌ ලබාදෙන ප්‍රතිපාදන යටතේ රු.
මිලියන 15.270ක මුදලක්‌ වැය කරන ලදී. එය පිළිවෙලින්‌ ගාල්ල දිස්ත්‍රික්කය සඳහා රු. මිලියන 1.327ක්ද, මාතර
දිස්ත්‍රික්කය සඳහා රු. මිලියන 12.500ක්ද, හම්බන්තොට දිස්ත්‍රික්කය සඳහා රු. මිලියන 1.373කි. මෙම රොග මර්ධනයට
හා පැතිරීම වැළැක්වීමට පොල්‌ වගාකරුවන්‌ දැනුවත්‌ කිරීමේ වැඩසටහන්‌ පැවැත්වීම පමණක්‌ නොව නව ව්‍යාපෘති හා
සංවර්ධන කටයුතු මගින්‌ විශාල පිටුවහලක්‌ වගාකරුවන්‌ වෙත ලබා දී ඇත.

පොල්‌ වගා කිරීමේ මණ්ඩලය මගින්‌ ක්‍රියාත්මක කරනු ලබන පොල්‌ වගාකරුවන්‌ අතර ප්‍රචලිත ව්‍යාපෘතියක්‌ වන කප්රුක
ආයෝජන ණය යොජනා ක්‍රමය මඟින්‌ රු. මිලියන 308.26 ක්‌ වසර පුරා වගා හිමියන්ට සහනදායී පදනමක්‌ මත ණය මුදල්‌
ලබාදීමත්‌ ලබාගත්‌ ණය වෙනුවෙන්‌ බැංකු අය කළ පොලියට සාපේක්ෂව රු. මිලියන 15.073 සහන පොලියක්‌ ද ආපසු

ලබා දී ඇත.

ස්වයං මුල්‍ය ඒකකයක්‌ 2010.12.31 දනට තවාන්‌ හා සංවර්ධන අංශය රු. මිලියන (30.128) ක ඌනනතාවයක්ද මීගමුව බිජ
නිෂ්පාදන ඒකකය රු. මිලියන (20.735)ක සේවා වියදමක්ද දරා ඇති අතර, ආදර්ශ පොල්‌ උයන්‌ මඟින්‌ රු. මිලියන
5.532 ක අතිරික්තතාවයක්‌ උපයා ඇත. පොල්‌ වගාකිරීමේ මණ්ඩලයේ 2010 වර්ෂය තුළ සමස්ථ මෙහෙයුම්‌ වලට අදාළව
රු. මිලියන 33,4585ක විවිධ ආදායමක්‌ උපයා ගැන්මට හැකි වී තිබේ. 2010 වර්ෂයේ සමස්ථ අතිරික්තය රු. මිලියන

පොල්‌ වගාකිරීමේ මණ්ඩලය

පොල්‌ වගාකිරීමේ මණ්ඩලය 2019 දෙසැම්බර්‌ 31 දිනෙන්‌ අවසන්‌ වර්ෂය සඳහා වූ මූල්‍ය ප්‍රකාශන
ඇතුළත්ව එගි කටයුතු පිළිබඳව 1071 අංක 38 දරන මුදල්‌ පනතේ 13 (7 එගන්තිය ප්‍රකාරව
සභාපනිවෙත ඉදිරිපත්‌ කරන විස්තරාත්මක විගණකාධිපති වාර්තාව.

(අ)

විගණන නිරීක්ෂණය

තනොග සමීක්ෂණ වාර්තා අනුව
සමාලෝවිත වර්ෂයේ ආරම්භක තොග
අයිතමයක (පොලිබෑග්‌ වටිනාකම
ර.1,200,6000 ක්‌ අඩුවෙන්මූල්‍ය
ප්‍රකාශන වල ගලපා තිබීම නිසා වර්ෂයේ
මෙහෙයුම්‌ අතිරික්තය එමප්‍රමාණයෙන්‌
වැඩියෙන්මූල්‍ය ප්‍රකාශන වල දක්වා
තිබුණ. එසේම ඉකුන්‌ වර්ෂයේ උපවිත
වියදම්‌ අධි වෙන්කිරීම සමාලෝවිත
වර්ෂයේ ලාහයට ගැලපීමකින්‌ නොරව
ඉකුත්‌ වර්ෂ ගැලපුම්‌ ලෙස දක්වා නිබීම
නිසා වර්ෂයේ අතිරික්තය රුැ.1, 137.131
ක්‌ අඩුවෙන්‌ මූල්‍ය ප්‍රකාශනවල දක්වා

කර්මාන්ත අමාත්‍යංශයෙන්‌ ලැබිය යුතු                                      ගැනීමට කටයුතු කළ

2010 ප්‍රාග්ධන ඇස්තමේන්තුවෙන්‌ පලෙයි

විය. කෙසේ වුවද සාමාන්‍ය වෙළඳපලේදී

කළමනාකාරීත්වයේ අදහස්‌ දැක්වීම

පලෙයි සම්පත්‌ මධ්‍යස්ථානයට අවශ්‍ය
භාණ්ඩ මිල දී ගැන්මේ දී අවශ්‍යතාවය,
පමිතිය, කල්පැවැත්ම, නිමාව යන සියලූ
කරුණු සලකා බලා තාක්ෂණික ඇගයීම්‌
කමිටු නිර්දේශ ද සහිතව විධිමත්‌ ප්‍රසම්පාදන
ක්‍රමවේදයට අනුකුලව මිල දී ගැනීම සිදු කර
ඇති බව සදහන්‌ කරම්‌.

කෙසේවුව ද, ඉදිරියේ දී ඇස්තමේන්තු
සකස්‌ කිරිමේ දී හා මිල දී ගැනීම සිදු කිරිමේ
දී සකසුරුවම්ව කටයුතු     කිරිමට
සැලකිලිමත්‌ වන බව කාරුණිකව සදහන්‌
කරම්‌.

Annual Report 201°

Targets

e Increasing the yicld of coconut by increasing the population of coconut palms
to ensure the sustainability of the yield to meet the demand of the coconut
consumers and processors.

© Increasing the productivity of coconut lands and farm income through animal
husbandry / intercrop diversification

© Formulate the smallholder in to community-based organization, create
employment opportunity and eliminate poverty in order to focus on medium
Scale and Small-scale coconut related industries in coconut cultivation.

e Enhance organic and inorganic fertilizer application to ensure Sustainable
coconut cultivation

e Toincreasc the annual coconut production to 3000 million nuts by 2020 to
meet consumption and industrial demand of the country.

e Toupgrade all the coconut plantation to model coconut gardens of the

Coconut Cultivation Board ensuring increase of profitability by 20% by 2020

Objectives

e nhance Technical knowledge and skills of coconut cultivation to every market
grower
Maintain a demand driven extension Service and provision of high quality inputs
Establishment of Sustainable Coconut Cultivation in Sri Lanka
Promote utility of coconut lands by cultivating intercrops suitable for coconut

e lands

Implement **Kapruka Puruwara program” island wide

Promote the use of organic and inorganic fertilizer application

Promote soil and water conservation in coconut lands

Reduce damage pests and diseases damages to coconut cultivation

Use of Model Coconut Gardens of Coconut Cultivation Board to educate
growers

e Enhance domestic coconut production required for domestic consumption,
oconut based products and foreign markets



Introduction

The Coconut Cultivation Board was established by an order issued by the Minister of Plantation
Industries, published in the Gazette Notification dated 30" March 1072 under Section 02 ofthe Coconut

Development Ordinance No. 46 of 1071 aiming at development of coconut cultivation in the island.

This report includes operational activities of the Coconut Cultivation Board during the period from O01

January 201° to31 December20190.

Functions of the Board in terms of the aforesaid Act are described as follows;

e Increase and support to increase yield of coconut in cultivated lands

e Cultivation of coconuts in the lands, execute promotional initiatives, assist in formalization, Selection
of coconut cultivated lands suitable for intercropping from other cultivations (including grass) and
promotion, guidance, maintenance and support to maintain the intercropping program in coconut
cultivated lands.

e Enhance, regulate, cngageandextend supportanimal husbandry in coconut cultivated lands

e Describe, popularize, promote and guide the cffective cultivation methods related to the cultivation of
coconut and other crops in coconut cultivated lands.

othe coconut industry and train the advisory and extension officers

© Extend supportt

Pewee

Message from the Chairman

The Coconut Cultivation Board entitles a renowned place among the few state institutions among the few number
of State institutions that arc close to hearts of the people in the Democratic Socialist Republic of Sri Lanka.
Currently, the Coconut Cultivation Board is one ofthe mosttalked about political and media institutions.

However, the 40 year history of the Coconut Cultivation Board in the midst of various challenges, 2010 was yet
another year completed successfully. Coconut Cultivation Board had been allocated Rs. 700 million for 2010 and
bythe end ofthe ycar a sum of Rs. 56S had been received.

In the year 2019, the Board was able to distribute approximately 02 million high quality recommended coconut
Seccdlings to the coconut growers, island wide. The coconut Seedlings were distributed among the beneficiaries
under various subsidy schemes, which enabled them to add another 30,000 acres of coconut cultivations to the
island. Coconut growers were encouraged to increase the productivity in 6016 acres of existing coconut lands
through various rehabilitation relict programs implemented with the investment about Rs. 5. Million.

The Coconut Cultivation Board enrich with a Robust Extension Mechanism island wide, through which various
awareness programs are being carried out to empower the coconut growers. Further, the Board has been able to
provide pesticides, pheromones and predatory mites required for pest control without any shortage, island wide.

The Coconut Cultivation Board was able to lead the nurserics and model coconut gardens to enhance greater
productivity by encouraging value-added products in addition to their routinc products. Fcedbacks on Services
rendered by resorts established in various parts of the country imply that resorts have become popular destinations
for local and foreign tourists.

Control of Weligama coconut leaf wilt disease (WCLWD), mapping of major pests in coconut cultivations and
distribution of Mite Parasite Packets are major projects amongst the several other special projects launched in
2010 and such projectresulted in positive impacts.

New recruitments were made to fill number of vacancies existed in the Board and a number of promotions were
also granted. Number of local and foreign training programs and employee welfare activities were conducted
upon the theme of" Employee satisfaction enhances Productivity ofthe Institution’.

Overall, all development programs have positively contributed to great progress in 201° and Tam pleased to state
that the advice and guidance of Staff of the Ministry including the Minister of Plantation Industries, State
Minister Secretary to the Ministry and the active support rendered by staff of the Coconut Cultivation Board have
becn instrumental in this progress.

Palitha Pelpola,
Chairman,
Coconut Cultivation Board



NIessage from the General Manager

The Coconut Cultivation Board is also one of the most significant government institutions established for coconut
cultivation, which is as important as the coconut crop is to the people of SriLanka,

One of the main objectives of the Coconut Cultivation Board is to protect both local coconut growers and
consumers. New Strategies nced to be put in place to control increase in coconut prices within the country
fluctuations in coconut production due to climate change and the due to the increase in exports of coconut
products. New development programs were implemented in 201° focusing on increasing the land extent of new
coconut cultivation and increasing yield ofexisting coconut plantations.

In 2010, 1,024,906 high quality recommended coconut secdlings produced at nurserics of coconut cultivation
board have been issued to new, replanting, underplanting and for home gardens. It is expected that about 30,000
acres of new coconut plantations will be added to the list of coconut lands in the island.

Asum of Rs. 42.04 has becn spent on rehabilitation of Coconut Lands, moisture conservation, intercropping and
pipe born water facilities to increase the coconut yield in existing cultivation Measures have been taken to upgrade
3874 acres of land and actions were taken to develop 2742 acres under the Kapruka Investment Loan Program.

The Board has spent about Rs. 24,6032 Million for “Wevili Saviya Trained Manpower Project”, Mite Parasite
Packet Distribution Project, project for mapping insect damage on coconut cultivation that were implemented as
External Coconut Cultivation Development Projects that were amongst the development programs implemented
by the Coconut Cultivation Board thereby abled to achieve a great physical progress.

Plantation Saviya Training Manpower Project out of the active development programs, The Mite Parasite Packet
Distribution Project has spent about Rs. 24,632 Mn.

Control program of Weligama coconut leaf wilt disease (WCLWD) that is prevalence in Galle, Matara and
Hambantota Districts was successfully implemented during this year at a cost of Rs. 14,630,500.

In 2010, in addition to the traditional products of nurserics and model coconut gardens, actions were taken to
enhance value-added products to achieve higher yiclds on the land and gained , a profit of Rs. 5.5 Million.

Coordinated local, foreign, external and internal training programs and workshops for all employees,
Streamlining the human resource activities of the organization, thereby enhancing the knowledge and attitudes of
the employees and steps were taken to fill the vacancies prevailed at the Board.

Due to the favorable weather conditions for coconut cultivation experienced in 201°, the annual coconut harvest
was as high as 3106 million nuts, which is close to our annual coconut harvest targct. However, 201° was another
fruitful and successful year for the Coconut Cultivation Board. The advice and guidance of Hon. Minister of
Plantation Industries, State Minister, Secretary to the Ministry was very crucial for that success we gained. Talso
gratefully acknowledge the support and guidance of the Board of Directors, including the Chairman of the
Coconut Cultivation Board.

R. A.D. S.Ranathunga,
General Manager,
nut Cultivation Board



Coconut Cultivation Board in briet......

In order to develop the coconut industry throughout the island and to achieve
good productivity results in accordance to the vision and mission of the Board, the
Board consists of 10 regional offices, 265 coconut development officers ranges, 3

coconut development training centres, 3° nurseries, 12 coconut model gardens and

a seed production unit

Coconut Cultivation Board

Extension and Development Programs of
Coconut Cultivation Board

Major Development Programs and Extension Programs of the Coconut Cultivation Board are imple-

mented directly by the Extension and Development Division. Regional Offices have becn established at the

regional level under the direct supervision of the Deputy General Manager of Extension and Development Di-

vision. This service is provided to the coconut growers through the extension staff consisting of Coconut De-

velopment Officers. According to the Annual Action Plan, subsidy programs are implemented as follows.

=> Planting coconut seedlings under formal coconut cultivation

Under this subsidy, coconut growers will be provided coconut Seedlings frec of charge for new cultivation,

under cultivation or replanting and thus coconut seedlings are provided for cultivation from minimum acreage

of Va acre to maximum of 15 acres. The Seedlings are also transported to the grower and the Coconut Cultiva-

tion Board provides technical advice on planting and maintenance before distribution of the seedlings. The

program aimed at planting 762,800 coconut seedlings and however the Coconut Cultivation Board managed to

plant 702,211 coconut seedlings, in 2010. Under this program, coconut growers can buy a ground plant worth
Rs. 175 "= for Rs. 50 / = and a potted plant worth Rs. 250 / = at a concessionary price of Rs. 125 / =. Accord-

ingly, the subsidy value of a ground coconut seedling and a potted coconut seedling was Rs. 125 /=.

=> Maintaining an optimal number of coconut palms by planting

In most cases, failure to maintaining the optimal number of coconut palms in a coconut land is identified
as the main reason for decline in coconut productivity in coconut cultivated lands in Sri Lanka. The target
number of seedlings for desertification under coconut land rehabilitation in 2010 was 1,905,960. By the end
of 2010, 1,098,884 coconut seedlings were planted under this program. A grower can purchase a ground
plant worth Rs. 175 ” = for Rs. 50 / = and a potted plant worth Rs. 250 / = at a concessionary price of Rs.
125 =. Accordingly, the subsidy value of a ground coconut seedling and a potted coconut seedling was
Rs. 125 /=.

Programs to increase productivity of coconut lands and coconut cultivation

Under this program, subsidies are provided to the coconut growers under several methods to achieve the
objectives of increasing the coconut yicld in the short and long term and improving the living standards of
the coconut farmers by increasing the productivity of coconut lands and coconut cultivation. Accordingly,

the following subsidy programs were implemented.

Rchabilitation of coconut lands under various rehabilitation schemes

Subsidics are granted to the farmers for the following agronomic activitics;

e Construction of hull pits to ensure moisture conservation in coconut lands
e Construction of stone ridges and contour drains for soil conservation

e Application of organic manure for coconut cultivation

e Maintenance of fertilizer circle and mulching

e Application of dolomite to coconut tree

A maximum sum of Rs. 12,000 per acre is granted as subsidies to the grower to perform the above crop culti-
vation initiatives. In 2010, it was targeted to rehabilitate 6000 acres of coconut whereas the Board managed to
achieve a progress of 2797 acres and financial progress of Rs.22.63 Mn. at the end of the year.

Subsidy program for Piped water

Frequent and constant supply of water is required to coconut palm to protect it from drought and ensure higher
yiclds. Accordingly, the Coconut Cultivation Board implemented a subsidy scheme to establish water supply
Systems in the coconut land to protect the coconut cultivation under adverse climatic conditions.

Under this, subsidies were provided for the piped water supply systems recommended by the Coconut Re-
Search Institute for low cost irrigation. A maximum subsidy of Rs. 20,000 was provided to establish a water
Supply system for an acre of coconut.

The physical target and estimated cost for the construction of pipe water supply systems in coconut lands in the
year 2010 were 200 acres and Rs. 5.20 million respectively whereas at the cnd of the year, 721 acres and Rs.
10.63 million were reported as the progress against the target, respectively.

“Wevili Saviya’”’ Trained Manpower Proiect

The Extension System of providing inputs required to grower for coconut cultivation 1s, in most of the
cases, being implemented by the Coconut Cultivation Board. In addition to this methodology, the ““Wevili
Saviya” Trained Manpower Project is implemented with the intension of providing a convenient and clos-
cr extension service to the growers through trained farmers.

Im year 2010, the ““Wevili Saviya” trained workers were introduced to 3074 coconut lands and the
knowledge gained by them was replicated for the development of the relevant coconut lands, under this
context. A sum of Rs. 9.70Mn. has been invested for this purpose.

Sharing information with the coconut growers through SMS methodology

SMS service was launched in 2010 with the objective of extending the expansion activities of the Coconut
Cultivation Board to the growers. Through this, the Coconut Cultivation Board was able to send 13 text
messages to 5055 growers in 20190.

Imtegrated Coconut Mite Control Program in the Coconut Triangle
Covering all Regional Office Areas, 355,308 Predatory Mite Packets were distributed under the Integrated

Coconut Mite Control Program, in 2019. Growers had the opportunity to obtain predatory mite parasite
packets at a concessionary price.

A special project was launched in 2010 aiming at controlling mites that make devastating impact on the
coconut harvest in Sri Lanka, distributing parasites in centralized production and ensuring storage facili-
ties at the Regional Offices of the Coconut Cultivation Board. Showing a remarkable financial progress of

Rs. 3.07 Mn storage facilities were upgraded to store mite parasite packets in 3 regional offices in the year
2010.

Annual Report 2010

227



Weligama coconut leaf wilt disease (WCLWD) control program

Weligama coconut leaf wilt disease (WCLWD) which was first reported from Weligama Divisional Secretar-
lat in Matara District in the Southern Province of Sri Lanka was later reported from Gallc and Hambantota Dis-
tricts. The disease is caused by a phytoplasma pathogen, which is very similar to a virus and no cure has been
found for phytoplasma in any country in the world.

Following the detection of the disease, the Coconut Research Institute in collaboration with the Director Gen-
eral of Agriculture, the lcgal authority for the implementation of the Plant Protection Act, has designated 408
Grama Niladhari Divisions in the Matara, Hambantota and Galle Districts as Discase Zones.

Likewise, a region with the length of 86 km and width of 3 km along the road from Galle Deniyaya to Tan-
Galle via Hakmana was designated as Disease Prevention Zone. All diseased trees in the region are uprooted
and it was prohibited to transport any biological material of the coconut trce outside the boundaries of the
zone, under the Plant Protection Act. The Department of Agriculture has also imposed a ban on the transporta-
tion of other crops belonging to this genus.

Since there are no other alternative measures to control the disease, the removal of diseased coconut trees
was Started in 2008 on the directions of the Coconut Research Institute. During 2010, the Coconut Culti-
vation Board has inspected 364 Grama Niladhari Divisions and identified 14680 diseased trees and of
which 0,938 discased trees have already been removed. A total amount of Rs. 14.03 Mn. has been paid as
compensation.

Extension prooram

The Coconut Cultivation Board, as an agricultural Service provider, must compulsorily provide extension infor-
mation on coconut cultivation to its client, the Coconut Grower. It 1s a key role of the Board. This is coordinat-
cd as follows;

Annual Action Plan and the relevant development plans as well as the plan for allocation of provisions in ac-
cordance with the overall corporate plan is formulated by the Assistant General Manager (Extension and De-
velopment) with the concurrence and supervision of

the Deputy General Manager of Extension and Development Division. Accordingly, all these information are
Sent in writing and by circulars to the Regional Offices and the Regional Managers implement development
and extension programs within their regions. In addition to the Rcgional Manager, Assistant Regional Manag-
crs, Extension Officers and Farm Planning Officers act as Supervisors. Under their total supervision, the exten-
Sion activities of the Coconut Development Officers and Ficld Officers are organized annually and monthly
basis while required fullest support. Provide resources and directions are provided by focal points of Coconut
Development Training Center.

Apart from this, Extension Services are rendered by Extension and Development Unit and Information Unit of
the Head Office at National Level.

implemented from 2017 to 2010. Under this, all maps related to the damage of coconut beetle, black beetle,
coconut mite and coconut caterpillar have been prepared. Financial progress of Rs. 6.117 Mn. has been

achieved under this program including purchase of cquipment related to the pest mapping program.

1.3. "Kapruka Aayoiana'’' Loan Scheme.

re
a.”

“Kapruka Aayojana” Loan Scheme is a concessionary loan scheme implemented by the Coconut Cultivation
Board since 1008 to provide financial assistance and technical guidance to coconut growers on land develop-
ment with the participation of leading financial institutions in the country.

The loan scheme seeks the total development of the lands of the coconut growers, with the primary objectives
of promoting commercial agriculture in connection with the coconut lands, increasing the contribution of the
coconut cultivation sector to the development of the country and raising the income level of the coconut grow-
crs and employees in the Sector.

State owned banks such as Pcople's Bank, Bank of Ceylon, State Commercial Banks, Regional Development
Bank, SANASA Development Bank and National Development Bank, Development Banks and private com-
mercial banks such as Hatton National Bank, Seylan Bank, Commercial Bank, Sampath Bank and Union Bank
have joined hands with the Coconut Cultivation Board for this loan scheme. Private commercial banks contrib-
ute to the financing of loans as contractual partners.

This scheme provides financial assistance at concessionary interest rates for development activities related to
coconut land development such as replanting, new cultivation, land rchabilitation, intercropping, animal hus-
bandry, Sctting up of irrigation systems, purchase of agricultural machinery and cstablishment of intercropping
nurseries.

Through this, loan financial assistance at an interest rate of 0% is provided and growers who carry out Success-
ful development activities are given 100% interest relict in the first year and 50% in the second year to the fifth
year. This allows Successful growers to access financing at a lower interest rate, such as 3.7%.

Im conjunction with these loan financing, free technical consultancy Services and loan projects are be sct up,
which will also provide growers with additional services nceded to achieve development goals.

230

Annual Report 2010


A Sum of Rs. 3162.34 million has already been provided to 10,734 cultivators for the development of 57,580
acres of land by this loan scheme. According to the progress made in the year 2010, Rs. 308.26 million has
been provided to 503 cultivators for the development of 2751 acres of land. For this purpose, Rs. 318.07 mil-
lion has bcen provided to the rclevant financial institutions during this year and Rs. 15.07 million has been
paid as interest relief benefits to the growers. Progress has been made beyond the targets in many regional of-
fice areas. Thus, the overall progress relative to the targets has exceeded 100%. Progress made in comparison
to the targets in terms of regional office areas in the year 2010.

1.5. Coconut Development Training Center (CDTO)
Imtroduction

The Coconut Development Training Center is located at Bandirippuwawatta, Lunuwila, adjacent to the
Coconut Research Institute.

The main objective of establishing and maintaining the Coconut Development Training Center within the
Coconut Cultivation Board is to train the officers of the Coconut Cultivation Board. It provides the back-
drop for the cfficient and cffective transmission of coconut cultivation technology to coconut growers and
industrialists through the enhancement of the knowledge and skills of the Extension Officers, the most
important team of the Coconut Cultivation Board.

In addition, non-technical officers of the Coconut Cultivation Board are also trained at the Coconut De-
velopment Training Center through which Knowledge and skills of the said officers are cnhanced result in
human resource development of the institution ensuring conducive and necessary background to perform
the duties of the organization conveniently and cfficiently.

In addition to training the internal officers of the Coconut Cultivation Board, various targeted groups en-
gaged in the coconut industry are provided in-house training at Coconut Development Training Center
and further the training officers of the Coconut Development Training Center visit to required localities
to extend training facilities for teams and individuals with training nceds. The technology of coconut cul-
tivation 1s directly transmitted to them by enhancing their knowledge and skills by designing and imple-
menting training courses required for coconut development as required by the ficld.

Extension and training programs are carried out through the Coconut Development Training Center under
the comprehensive National Extension Program of the Coconut Cultivation Board. Under this, disease
and pest management programs and extension and media programs are also carried out continuously, un-
der this program

The Coconut Development Training Center conducts a miscellaneous Special programs on control of dis-
cases and pests in coconut cultivation. Special programs for control of red beetle, black beetle, mite, co-
conut caterpillar and Plecispa pests that are the main pests in coconut cultivation, are the most significant
programs amongst the special programs conducted by CDTC. In addition, the Coconut Development
Training Center also carries out the activities of Predatory Mite Factories and Coconut Caterpillar Labor-
atories Scattered island wide.

Preparation, printing, distribution of training tools such as leaflets, boards, posters and videos required for
extension and development programs and also carried out by Coconut Development Training Center.
prepares, prints and distributes training tools such as leaflets, boards, posters and videos required for ex-
tension and development programs. Further, the Coconut Development Training Center also conducts
extension and development programs and prepares, prints and distributes relevant forms required for
evaluation. The Coconut Development Training Center makes a direct contribution to national level out-
reach and media programs.

Coconut Development Training Center 1s an institution registered under the Tertiary and Vocational Edu-

cation Commission. Accordingly, the institute is professionally cligible to conduct courses and award
certificates.

=> Extension Methodology (Part D

It 1s paramount important the Coconut Development Officers, who are the srassroots officers of the Exten-
Sion Service of the Coconut Cultivation Board, be conversant with subject of extension Service as well as the
globally recognized extension methods in order to productive deploy them in service in the current context.
The Coconut Development Training Center implemented a series of training programs in 2010 and realizing

this objective.

The trainees were introduced to the concept of "New Extension Lead" and covered 7 skill modules contain in
the “New Extension Lead” training module.

Trainees were sensitized on the concept of agro-innovation, the role of extension and advisory Services in
agro-innovation System, history of extension Service, approaches of extension Service, extension methodolo-
gies, extension tools and accurate selection of extension tools in the aforesaid 7 training modules. The train-
ces were also trained on how to design, implement, direct and evaluate agricultural extension programs and
professional cthics, adult cducation methods, social psychology and behavioral changes that an extension of-

ficer should enrich with.

In addition, the training program covered thematic areas such as essential communication methodologies, Sig-

nificance of communication for innovation systems and facilitation for agricultural development. In addition

to the Coconut Development Officers, Farm Planning Officers were also accommodated for this program.

=» Extension Methodology (Part ID

This program focused on seven new skills modules in addition to the seven modules covered under Extension
Methodology Part 1. This created awareness on community mobilization, problem solving techniques, group
methodologies, farmer group activism and development. This training program pave foundation for the train-
ces to study on market behavior, market value chains and the relationship between farmers, agri-

entrepreneurship, business planning, financial management and the impact of gender issues on agribusiness

Services.

The main crop of the Model Coconut Garden is Coconut Cultivation but cultivation of intercrops, animal
husbandry, coir production, Copra Production, running tourist guest houses, coconut shell based charcoal
production, production of coconut husk chips, production of coconut oil, production of coconut scedlings,
production of intercrops plants, operation of Kapthurupaya outlets are carried out as income generation
project with the intension of optimizing the profits. Further, paddy cultivation, rubber cultivation, produc-
tion of predatory mite packets, coconut tourism project and Glyricidia cultivation projects were imple-
mented according to the potential of the model coconut gardens. Model Coconut Gardens are carried out
as demonstration unit as a profitable coconut based inductry.The Coconut Development Training Center
also conducts awareness programs for coconut growers, school children, university students, officials of
public and private institutions and members of societies in agricultural organizations. These model coco-

nut gardens also provide practical guidance and training to trainees on how to maintain coconut cultiva-

tion profitably.

The products of the model coconut gardens arc high quality sceds of coconut, coconut seedlings, curry

coconut, copra, coconut Shell charcoal, cow's milk, buffalo milk, yoghurt, milk toftce, cggs, vegetables,

fruits, spices, rubber, intercrops seedlings, paddy and Predatory mite packets are issued to the consumers.

2.1.1. Coconut Cultivation

In 2010, 6,406,300 coconuts have been harvested from Model Coconut Gardens. The harvest in 2018 was
4,701,605 nuts, an accordingly it was an increase of 1,704,704 nuts in 2010. The average production cost

of a nut in 2010 is Rs. 18.40. The average selling price of a nut is Rs. 23.64 and the average profit per nut
1s RS. 5.24.

The total income of coconut in the year 201° was Rs. 153,586,003.50 and the total expenditure was Rs.
110,550,749.25. Accordingly, the total profit was Rs. 34,026,254.34. Table 3 shows the 2010 Annual Tar-
gct, Progress, Total Revenue, Total Expenditure, Total Profit, Average Product Cost per Nut, Average

2.1.6. production of Coconut Husk Chips

Coconut Cultivation Board

Coconut chips could be used as a subsidiary to coir fiber pith in scedling production. Coconut husk chips is
produced from the coconut husk available at modern coconut gardens and used instead of coir fiber pith in
order to reduce the annual expenditure incurred for purchase of coir fiber pith while the excess production is

sold.

2.1.16. Organic Fertilizer Application

Organic manure is applied to the soil for long term improvement of the soil condition of the coconut plan-
tation by improving the physical condition of the soil, increasing its nutrient content and increasing the
functions of soil organisms. Poultry manure, cow dung, goat / sheep manure and compost are used as or-
ganic manure depending on the availability.

2.1.17. Imtercropping

2/3 of lands within the coconut cultivated lands saved due to the gap maintained in coconut cultivation
and the said saved lands could productively be utilized for other cultivations. More particularly, intercrop-
ping 1s viable in coconut cultivated lands less than 5 years and more than 35 years when the coconut 1S
cultivated as a mono-culture. Accordingly, short term crops and long term crops have been cultivated us-
ing the same space while existing intercrops have been maintained. Short term vegetables, potatoes,
herbs, spices, pulses, cereals and fruits have been cultivated as intercrops. Intercropping in the year 2010

has carned an income of Rs.2512036.00 yiclding a profit of Rs.504686.0>2.

2.2.1. Coconut Seedling Production and Issuance Program

Production of high quality coconut seedlings required for cultivation in the island and distribution amongst the
growers 1s one of the key roles of the Coconut Cultivation Board. Plan to supply of required coconut seed to
nurserics, operation and coordination, scedling production, as per the plan of extension and development divi-
Sion 1s carried out by Model Coconut Garden and Nursery Division. Regional Offices, Nurseries and Model

Coconut Gardens mainly contributes to Coconut Scedling Production.

Under the direct supervision and direction of Regional Managers and Residential Nursery Kecpers, high quali-
ty coconut Seedlings are produced by 3° nurseries that are the focal bodies for coconut seedling production
and by 12 nurseries cstablished with model coconut gardens that are managed under direct supervision and

directions of the manager of Model Coconut garden.

Coconut Scedling Nurseries are established island wide with the intension of case of access by the growers to
purchase required seedlings and most of such nurseries are established within North Western Province which
1s the main coconut production region in the island. Management nurseries is carried out by respective region-

al offices. Production of Coconut seedling by the Board in 201° is shown below;

Special Proiect implemented by Nursery Development Division - 2010

IPreparation of concrete nursery beds

Establishment of Concrete Bed which was recognized to be a result oriented method ( recording
germination percentage of 80%) by a test conducted in 2016, at Eraminiyagolla. This method re-
quires relatively lower quantity of water while reduces the cost that incur for content of soil mixture

used for potted plants.

Construction of safety house covered by nets for seedling production

A safety house for the production of fruits and export oriented seedling was constructed at Kirindiwe-

la with the intension of enhance the productivity of Nurseries and income.

° Organic Fertilizer Production

Compost fertilizer production was commenced in Nurseries established at Wennoruwa, Eraminiyagolla,
Uhana, Ibbagamuwa to use for fertilizer mix for potted seedling production, to Satisfy organic fertilizer
requirement for existing crops and to reduce the expenditure on chemical fertilizer.

© Preparation of coconut husk pits to protect moisture conditions.

Preparation of approximately 50 coconut husk pits to protect the moisture conditions of existing coconut

cultivation at Wennoruwa Nursery.

Establishment of new water supply system

° Deepening and cnlarging the water pit at Mayurapada Nursery ensuring water protection so as to ac-

quire water.

° Refurbishment of Agro-well at Achchuvely nursery, establishment of water sprinkle system and cstab-

lishment of tube well.

° Establishment low cost water sprinkle system for an extent of One Acre at Nurseries and nursery beds

at KAlaweva.

2.3. Negombo Coconut Seed Production Unit

The key role of the unit is to transport and supply of high quality coconut seedlings to all Nursery and Model
Coconut Gardens under the supervision of the Coconut Research Institute with the objective of providing high

quality coconut seedlings to growers for cultivation throughout the island.

Im addition to this, the other functions of this unit arc to contribute to the formulation of strategic plans to meet
the annual Seed and coconut requirements, to implement those plans, to facilitate and direct the input and Sup-
ply services required by the coconut growers. All thesc activities are carried out by the Seed Production Unit,

which has the necessary infrastructure and experienced field staff attached to it.

The number of coconut seedlings required for the coconut cultivation programs implemented in cach district
varies according to the regional offices, and the requirement of coconut Seedlings in the regional offices varies
depending on the demand for coconut seedlings by the growers in the areca. The Regional Managers inform the
Head Office of the need for coconut Seedlings in their area annually and supply the seeds to the Nursery ac-
cording to a plan prepared by the Head Office considering the coconut seedling requirement of the Regional

other roles of Negombo Seed Coconut Unit.

05. Finance Management Division

5. 1. Financial Statement

Overall Functions of the Coconut Cultivation Board In accordance with the provisions of the Coconut De-
velopment Act No. 46 of 1071, subject to the due circulars of monetary regulations in accordance with the
Fiscal Accounting Standards of Sri Lanka, the Financial Reports as at year ending on 31.12.2010 have been
Submitted.

The key process of the Finance Management Division is to prepare Financial Estimations, planning, opera-
tion and control, documentation, reporting and review so as at suit to achieve the targets of Nursery 3° and
Model Coconut Garden 12 that are within the network comprise with 10 regional offices island wide and 3
training centers and to implement national level development projects and programs.

Operational functions, reporting and governance of financial functions of island wide regional offices are
carried out by Assistant General Manager (Financial Management), Accountant (Finance), Accountant
(Model Coconut Garden), Accounts Officer and other support Staff under the operation and direction of the
Deputy General Manager (Financial Management).

The General Treasury has provided Rs. 460.00 million under Recurrent Expenditure com-
ponent and Rs. 568.00 million under Capital Expenditure component in relation to the
Board's estimates for the year 2019.

The Coconut Cultivation Board functions to carry out projects to uplift coconut cultivation on behalf of the
Ministry of Plantation Industries. Accordingly, a sum of Rs. 17.100 million to *“Kapruka Purawara Fund”,
Rs. 15.731 million for the control of coconut leaf wilt Disease, Rs. 15.855 million for the Pest Management
Mapping Project, 15.855 million for trained labor force project and Rs. 3.360 for Mite Control project have
been granted in 20190.

A sum of Rs. 15.270 million was Spent under the provisions provided by the Ministry of Plantation Indus-
tries to control coconut leaf wilt Disease, which has spread and prevalence in Galle Matara and Hambantota
districts. A sum of Rs. 1.373 million, Rs. 12.560 million and Rs. 1.373 million were spent for Galle, Matara
and and Hambantota districts, respectively.

Kapruka Investment Loan Scheme, implemented by the Coconut Cultivation Board and a popular project
amongst coconut growers, has granted a concessionary loan of Rs. 308.26 million to the growers through-
out the year and repaid a sum of Rs. 15.6073 million as interest concession.

Nursery and Development Division, a self-financing unit, has reported a deficit of Rs. (30.128) million,
Negombo Seed Production Unit has reported a service expenditure of Rs. (20.735) million and the Model
Coconut Garden had recorded a surplus of Rs. 5.532 million as at 31.12.2010. Coconut Cultivation Board
has carned a miscellaneous income of Rs. 33,458 million in relation to overall operational activities and
accordingly the Board has reported a surplus of Rs. 141.088 million in 2019.

Im 2010, total recurrent expenditure incurred by the Board was Rs. 584.010 million and a sum of Rs.
421.0106 has been granted as subsidies for the growers for extension and developmetal Services and Rs.
71.641 Million has been spent for procurement. Accordingly, the total value of the assets owned by the

Board is Rs. 2375.032 million.

Coconut Cultivation Board,

06. Auditor Generals Report

AUDITOR GENERAL'S REPORT

Comprehensive Auditor General's Report submitted to the Chairman in terms of Section 13 (7XA)
of Finance Act No. 38 of 1071 on the Coconut Cultivation Board's activities including financial

statements for the year ended on the 31 day of December 2019.

The audit of the Financial Statements of the Coconut Cultivation Board for the year ended 31
December 201° and its functions was carried out under my direction in pursuance of provisions in
Article 154 (1) of the Constitution of the Democratic Socialist Republic of Sri Lanka which should
concurrently be read with Section 13(1) of Finance Act No. 38 of 1071 and Orders of National
Audit Act No. 1° of 2018. This report is issued based on the outcome of the Audit carried out in in
pursuance of Section 13 (D(A) of the Finance Ac t{ No. 3§ of 1071.

L2 Responsibilities of management and controlling parties in respect of financial statements

It is the responsibility of the management to prepare these financial statements in accordance with the
Sri Lanka Accounting Standards and to make reasonable submissions to determine the internal
controls required to prepare financial statements without quantitative or misleading statements that

occur due to frauds and errors.

In preparing financial statements, it is the responsibility of management to determine the continuity
of the Board and to maintain accountability and disclosure of matters relating to the continued
existence of the Board unless the management intends to liquidate the Board and discontinue

operations when there is no other option.

Responsibility in relation to Financial Reporting Process of the Board is held by the Governing
Parties.

285

Annual Report 2010



In accordance with Sub-section 16 (1) of the National Audit Act No. 10 of 2018, the Bureau shall
maintain proper books and records on its income, expenditure, assets and liabilities in order to be

able to prepare annual and periodical financial statements.

In pursuant to the section 3° of the National Audit Act No. 1° of 2018, in case of any measures
Suggested with regard to the contents of this report, it is required to be notified to me before expiry

of three months from the date of this report.

1.3 Scope of the Audit

It is my objective to obtain reasonable assurance about whether the Financial Statements as a whole
are free from material misstatement, whether duc to fraud or crror, and to issue an auditor’s report
that includes my opinion. Reasonable assurance is a high level of assurance, but is not a guarantee
that an audit conducted in accordance with Sri Lanka Audit Standards will always detect a material
misstatement when it exists. Misstatements can arise from fraud or crror and are considered
material if, individually or in the aggregate, they could reasonably be cxpected to influence the

economic decisions of users taken on the basis of these Financial Statements.

As part of an audit in accordance with Sri Lanka Audit Standards, I do exercise professional

Judgment and maintain professional skepticism throughout the audit. Further,

e Identity and assess the risks of material misstatement of the Financial Statements, whether duc
to fraud or error, design and perform audit procedures responsive to those risks, and obtain
audit cvidence that is sufficient and appropriate to provide a basis for our opinion. The risk of
not detecting a material misstatement resulting from fraud is higher than for one resulting from
error, as fraud may involve collusion, forgery, intentional omissions, misrepresentations, or the

override of internal control.

° Obtain an understanding of internal control relevant to the audit in order to design audit
procedures that are appropriate in the circumstances, but not for the purpose of expressing an

opinion on the cffectiveness of the internal controls of the Board.

Conclude on the appropriateness of management's use of the going concern basis of accounting
and, based on the audit cvidence obtained, whether a material uncertainty exists related to
events or conditions that may cast significant doubt on the Board's ability to continue as a going
concern. If 1 conclude that a material uncertainty exists, Tam required to draw attention in our
auditor’s report to the related disclosures in the Financial Statements or, if such disclosures are
inadequate, to modify my opinion. My conclusions are based on the audit evidence obtained up
to the date of our auditor's report. However, future events or conditions may cause the Board

to cease to continue as a going concern.

2. Financial Review

2.1 Financial Results

Operational Results of the year reviewed was a surplus of Rs. 141,088,348 and the corresponding Surplus of the Year was Rs. 14,885,007. Accordingly, a growth
in Financial Results of Rs. 126,873,206 was observed. The main reason for growth in operation result had been the decrease in Development programs during the
year reviewed by Rs. 232,873,296 when compared with the previous year.

2.2. Ratio Analysis

The current ratio has been decreased from previous year to year reviewed from 1:2:50 to 1:2:47 Instant ratio has been increased from 1:0:50 to 1:0:66.The profit
ratio which was 1.3 percent in the previous year has increased to 14.1 per cent in the year reviewed. The main reason this scenario 1s the decrease in expenditure
on development program in the year reviewed.

07. Clarifications on Auditor Generals Report

Coconut
Auditor,
National

Auditors

Cultivation Board

Audit Office

Report submitted in terms of Section 12 of National Audit Act No. 10 of 2018 on financial

statements of the Coconut Cultivation Board for thc year ended on the 31*: day of December 2010.

Answers

L2.l.

Sri Lanka Public Sector Accounting Standards

(A)

Standard No. 07

@

In accordance with the accounting policies of Coconut Cultivation Board, all equipment such as furniture,
office equipment, computers and software are annually depreciated by 10% based on the assumption that
that equipment have 10 years of lifespan. Accordingly, Property Plant and Equipment of the Coconut
Cultivation Board has also been reported as “Furniture and Fitting” under Note No. 02 in the Financial
Statement. Coconut Cultivation Board is non-profit semi-governmental institution that provides service to
the general public. Accordingly, it 1s appropriate to account the value of furniture and office equipment for
a period of 10 years. Likewise, considering the computer software and clectric equipment, although
software get updated within a short period of time, hardware is utilized for a period over 05 years. Changes
in hardware could be reinstated as spare parts. Accordingly, it 1s appropriate to maintain these assets for a
period of 10 years and it is more effective for non-profit institutions. All assets such as furniture and fitting
have been stated under 10% depreciation rate in the financial statements. However, it is noted to separately

present furniture, office equipment, computer equipment in financial statement -2020.

(@D

Completion report with regard to construction of First Phase of New Building in Matale Regional Office
and solar power system established in the Head office are yet to be received by the Finance management
Division. Accordingly, actions will be taken to capitalize and depreciate the assets in accordance with the

work completion report. This assets have been accepted for year 2020 and accounted in the year 2020.

(iD

Coconut Cultivation Board 1s a public establishment engages in miscellaneous functions in the field of
coconut that comprise with 19 Regional Offices, 39 Seedling Nurseries, 12 Model Coconut Gardens and
02 Coconut Development Training Centers island wide in order to increase the national coconut
production. Assets are maintained under several items to realize the said functions. Although the
depreciated net value of those asset is One Rupee, those assets have not been revalued based on the life
span. It would cost rupees millions to accomplish the revaluation. Those expenses should be recovered by
provisions of the treasury. Although it has been highlighted by the said Standard, since Coconut
Culuivation Board is a non-profitable service oriented establishment, carrying out valuation in 10 year

interval and recognition of depreciation would be an increase of capital expenditure of the government.

Annual Report 2010

307



Therefore, capital expenditure and generation of capital profit 1s accomplished by the government
expenditure. Accordingly, it has been noted to take action to review the effective lifespan of assets after

estimating these expenditures for the next year and obtaining the approval of the minister for the same.

is)              Standard No. 02

Having rectified the documentation faults from Standard No. 02(B) (0 to (1%) m the Financial Statements,
Amended Finance Flow Statement has submitted for the Audit.

a           Standard No. 11

Although Capital Expenditure received from the Treasury as government provisions, is accounted as
Capital Expenditure in the relevant year, the ministry rants funds for projects having treated that such
prolect are of the Ministry. Thus, said expenditure 1s accounted in relevant expenditure line items of the
Ministry. But, the funds received by the Board from external parties are considered as revenue of the year
concerned. Subsequently, those expenses will be accounted on how such expenditure is incurred.
Adjustment and cut off of Annual Depreciation on procurement and construction is met by provisions from
the Treasury. Therefore, if capital purchases from other projects are done in accordance with Standard No.
11. it may be reduced from the government provisions receivable to the Board. Therefore, since the funds
received for projects either from the Ministry or from other parties are not considered as Government

Grants, it has not been accounted in terms of Standard No. 11.

La       Accounting Deficiencies

(@       A sum of Rs.5,806.,735/- out of Rs. 31,516.160/= being the amount duly estimated by Land Reclamation
Commission and approved by Coconut Cultivation Board for the Model Coconut Garden of Pasikuda, has
been paid the balance amount of Rs. 25,7090.42425 has been accounted as at 31.12.2018 in favor of
account of Passikudah General Ledger — Account Code — 2222 — PAS by Journal No. 353 to the Tax
Provision Account of Land Reclamation Commission. Further. it has been disclosed under Provision for
L.R.C. Tax — MG 25,837.424.25 under Note No. 17 in the page No. 20 of the Finance Report ended on
31.12.2018. Further, this value has also disclosed under Note No. 17 mm the page No. 20 of the Finance
Report ended on 31.12.2019.( copies of relevant documents have been attached hereof) (Annexes from O01
to 05)

Likewise, an amount of Rs. 40,060 has been paid as Tax for Passikudah Model Coconut Garden as per the

invoice given by Land Reclamation Commission.

(DD       As per the Stock Survey, since the value of empty Poly Bags relevant to Coconut Seedling Ledger has
been understated by Rs. 1,209,600 as at 31.12.2018 and the associated fault of understating the profit of
Nursery has not been adjusted, even as at 31.12.2010 by mistake. Action will be taken to rectify this
mistake finance statement of 2020

(0      Accrued Expenditure Excess or Negative Allocations in the Preparation of Financial Statements of the
Coconut Cultivation Board are adjusted to the adjustment account for the previous year. Action will be

taken to correct this error in the 2020 financial statements during the year under review.

(QD       Purchase of poly bags worth of Rs. 10/= has not been double entered in the cash book. But in the year

credited to the current account (1647). This error was noted for correction in the 2020 financial statements

Coconut Seedling produced at the Model Coconut Gardens of the Coconut Cultivation Board also
distributed on Subsidy basis. Likewise, Seed coconut produced at Model Coconut Gardens are distributed
amongst the nurseries for Coconut Seedling production and this activity has happened even in 2015. The
value of the coconut seedlings that are provided on subsidy basis, is given to the Coconut Cultivation
Board by Treasury Provisions. Therefore, value of all coconut seedling that are provided free of charges or
half rate to the grower by the Regional Offices is valued to the selling price and double entered in the
Income of coconut in Nursery Ledger and account as an expenditure of Development initiatives in the
Main Ledger. Thus subsidy coconut seedling income shown in the nursery Ledger also includes the value
of the coconut seedling issued from the Model Coconut Gardens. This transaction is not executed by cash.
That is, value of coconut seedlings issued to Regional Offices by Model Coconut Gardens are accounted as

follows:

Model Coconut Garden Ledger

Nursery Ledger Control Account — 1641                   Credit

Coconut Seedling Income Account -1013 Debit (for cach Model Coconut Garden)

Nursery Ledger

Coconut seedling purchasing account of Model CG  - Credit

Garden Ledger Control Account                                          - Debit

In 2015, the above notes relating to Mahayaya, Passikudah, Desivalley, Lenawa and Bopitiya Model
Coconut Gardens have been correctly accounted, when preparing the Model Coconut Garden Journal
No. 461, double entries of Gurtland, Randeniya, Mundel, Karmakermny and Kohombana Model Coconut
Gardens are not correct. That 1s, a Receivable account has been created in the Model Coconut Garden
Ledger and accounted notes.( Annex 13) Accordingly, the value of Rs. 34.971.,843.41 has been brought
forward due to an accounting deficiency. Accordingly it was noted down to take relevant action to cut
oft this amount agamst the profit carned by the Coconut Seedling Nursery of Self Finance Unit of the

Coconut Cultivation Board in next year'years.

03

Other observations

@

Required directions on data collection and updating for Mite damage has been circulated by the circular
No. CCB/CirculExt & Dev/2020 — 6 and dated 22.01.2020 (Mite Damage Management

Project.Relevant information are bemg gathered by Coconut Development Officers.

(

Demand for predatory Mite from coconut growers had rapidly increased by the year 2018, and since the
predatory Mite application was found to be crucial for the cultivation, it was identified that there was an

issue relating to transport predatory mite to the growers.

Accordingly in 201y, a special project proposal was submitted to the Treasury to formulate a
methodology for transportation of predatory mite to the growers in 2018 and to establish air-conditioned
store facility where there are no laboratories. Accordingly, the Treasury allocated provisions for the said

project for the years 2019, 2020 and 2021.

Likewise, in response to the said special project, currently store facilities have been established in the
ares of Anuradharura, Polonnaruwa, Marawila, Mundel. and actions are bemg taken establish store
facilities in the Regional Offices in Galle, Kalutara, Kuliyapitiya, and Trincomalee and Madhu Nursery

and Lunuwila Training Center.

Provisions have been given at the rate of Rs. 3/= for cach Mite Bag for the purpose of transportation and
the Regional Manager have been advised to use the available vehicles of the respective Regional Offices
or to hire vehicles on rental basis subject to follow formal procurement procedures in case of non-

availability of vehicles in the Regional Office.

Predatory Mite was produced in 11 laboratories by the Coconut Cultivation Board deploying the trained
new officers. In this context, there may be infections in different circumstances at different magnitudes

and volumes.

The scenario can take place due to different causes and sometimes could be identified in advance and

also there may instances where 1t cannot be identified.

Viz, there are no laboratories comprised with high quality sophisticated sterilization equipment, these
laboratories are designed with minimal facilities and production could be made at lower production cost
in order to provide predatory mite at a reasonable price to the coconut growers. Another issue encounter
by these laboratories 1s that, in most of the cases, the trained staff tum over in short span of time

whereby other staff are given short period of one month training and deploy in service.

Annual Report 2010

315



This process 1s carried out under close supervision of Trained Specialist (Pathologist) of our institution

and officers of Coconut Research Institute.

This infection persisted for a short period in other laboratories including laboratories in Batticaloa,
Kegalle and Amrpara. The said mfection was successfully controlled in all the areas except from

Welipitiya.

But, it was fount difficult to control the infection that took place in Welipitiya on frequent basis, where
officials of Coconut Research Institute and officers of our institute collectively carried out an research on
this matter and concluded that situation is caused by a fungus that exist in the wall of this old building

and special characteristic in the so1l in and around this premises.

Production activities were stopped in the laboratory as per the recommendation oft the officers and
currently the production 1s obtained from ““Handapanagala Laboratory” which 1s located in the close

proximity

(QD          Since the payment of Rs. 386,000.00 which was paid during the year reviewed for operational tax 1s a
recurrent cost, this amount should be paid to an external party named “Color Target Institute” by People
Bank Account No. 971 by which the Treasury recurrent expenses are bemg paid. However, since the
said account did not have adequate funds at this moment, it has been paid by Capital Fund No. 975 upon
the basis of reconcile the amount between the accounts. There are plenty of instances where these type of
transactions are Carried out on transferring funds from one account to another by reconciliation. But it
was discovered that the relevant officer had not taken steps to produce the cheque that was issued by
Account No. 971 to Account No. 975, to the relevant bank. Currently the subject clerk and the
Accounting officer-in-charge of the subject have left the Board, it was not able to locate the said cheque,
so far. Although all the document that had been under the custody of those two officer, 1t was discovered
that the said cheque had not been entered. The cheque issued by the Account No. 271 has neither been
submitted to the bank nor been reconciled. The said cheque had been drawn so as to be matured in 60
days.

Since the cheque has been issued 6 months ago, considering it as a valid cheque and has been re-entered
as ‘receipt’ in No. 971 account. Although the said cheque has been misplaced, in general, this type of

misplacement does not take place. This is the only occasion of occurrence of this type of incident.

There is no financial loss to the Board and there is no over payment from the account of Account No.
075. Actions will be taken to rectify this issue of financial transaction between relevant accounts, in
2020.

(න          Although the Board requested required provisions from the Treasury in 2014, since the Board was able
to receive only a sum of Rs. 7,000.,000.00 from the treasury, the anticipated activity could not be
accomplished as planned during the year. In accordance with the provision of Rs. 6.88.850.00 from the
2015 budget to build an Annex (additional building space), the procurement initiatives have been

completed and the work was assigned to the consultancy agency.

Thereinatfter, the Consultancy Agency has carried out the site supervision and existing building and
subsequently has submitted the bidding documents including Bill of Quantity (BoQ) and Construction
Plan. Actions are being carried out to get the approval for the Construction Design formulated by the
Consultancy Agency and duly filled application has been forwarded to the Urban development
Authority. Approval for the existing Building, lay out plan were also required to be submitted to the
Urban development Authority. Since the construction should be completed durmg this year and
simultaneously procurement activities to select a suitable contractor have been completed, the contract
award was granted while the Urban Development Authority was attending to issue the Development
License for the construction. Accordingly, the Coconut Cultivation Board happened to enter in to an

agreement with the contractor.

Accordingly, the Contractor commenced the relevant activities and subsequent to obtaining the soil
sample test report for pillmneg foundation depicted in the Bill of Quantity, the relevant Test Pile test has
been carried out. Steel Structure of the front elevation and construction of roof have been completed and

functions relating to finishing work are pending.

Since the contractor has not being able to continue the construction, several reminders have been served
to the contractor. Focusing on the final conditions produced by the contractor and based on the
conditions that could be applied for the client three months of extension for the contract has been given
to the contractor following formal procurement conditions recommended by the consultant.
Accordingly, the contractor has formally informed the Coconut Cultivation Board that they would attend
the construction work, complete it and hand over the assignment within the period of Three (03) months.
However, since the contractor continuously failed to commence the construction work as agreed and
failure to extend the Performance bond, the Board with the recommendation of the Consultant, taken

steps to take over the said performance Security to the Board.

Although a discussion had been scheduled to make decision on the construction and as the contractor
failed to attend the said discussion, a discussion was held with the participation of officers of the
consultancy agency and construction institute. Thereby the Contractor Institution agreed to complete the
front area of construction and to take action to pay the losses to the Board in case of any loss incurred.

However, actions were taken to serve a comprehensive letter inclusive of all details to the Attomey

General through the Ministry and it is expected to take actions upon the directions.

In accordance with the Management Service Circular No. 03/2018, since staff recruitment or decision on
salary and allowance for the staff did nit accomplished at that moment, as per the directions of the
chairman, actions have been taken to duly advertise those vacancies in newspaper publications and other
public notifications as a pre-preparedness, until the approval shall be granted. Accordingly, I do state
that the Orders of Management Service Circular No. 03/2018 have not been breached. (This description
was prepared quoting the letter My No: EHRD/TIAU/’Auditor General'2019 and dated 13.03.2020)

This program was launched to address the issue of lack of trained laborers in the field of coconut
cultivation. There should be trained laborers who could handle agro-equipment and machineries fluently
amongst the trained laborers. It is paramount important to have relevant agro-tools, machineries to

provide the said training and required the field equipment and electro traning supplements. Practical

31838

Annual Report 2010


applications of these tools and equipment by the laborers will enhance the capacity of laborers to handle
those equipments. Further, Tabs and other field-based equipment were purchased in order to

complement to skills development of the laborers.

Purchase of Tabs under this project was done in order to use them as electrical equipment to conduct
training. Coconut Development Officers use those tabs in provision of training for the laborers. Since the
targeted trainee possess lower education level these tabs and demonstrations are used to effectively and
attractively conduct the training. Thus, these tabs are effectively used by the Coconut Development
Officers to create videos, Mobile Apps, other demonstrations to enhance technical knowledge of the

laborers.
